&ANK/STRESSAnkle Talar Tilt Stress Test:
-- Contralateral ankle used for comparison
-- Line is drawn across the talar dome and tibial vault
-- Normal talar tilt angle is less than 5 deg
-- Lateral ligament tears: ATFL & CFL

----------
< Book: The Unstable Ankle, by Meir Nyssa>


Rubin and Witten (1984): normal range of talar tilt up to 23'', altuough over 20'' was unusual.
Seldin (1960): normal range of up to 14'' with a side-to-side difference of 10''
Berridge and Bonnin (1944): talar tile of up to 25'' in 5% of the population.
Bonnin (1940, 1970) uninjured patients with a talar tile of 5'' to 15'' as having a hypermobile ankle.
Rechtime et al (1982), Silver & Deutsch (1982): side-to-side difference in the talar tilt of up to 5''
Canale (1980), Evans & Frenyo (1979): side-to-side difference in the talar tilt of up to 10''
Freeman (1965): side-to-side difference in the talar tilt of up to 6''



Clanton and Schon (1993): a normal anterior translation ranging from 2 to 9 mm
Brostrom et al (1965), Karlsson & Anderson (1992), Renstrom & Konradsen (1997): anterior talar translation of 10 mm or side-to-side difference of 3 mm as pathologic

&BALTHAZARBalthazar Scoring:
CT severity index = CT grade point + points for necrosis
Grade Points

Gr A (0) – normal CT
Gr B (1) – focal or diffuse enlargement of the pancreas
Gr C (2) – pancreatic gland abnormalities and peripancreatic inflammation
Gr D (3) – fluid collection in a single location
Gr E (4) – two or more collections and/or gas bubbles in or adjacent to pancreas

Necrosis percentage Points:
No necrosis -- 30% -- 50% --
0 2 4 6
&BOSNIAKBosniak Classification of Renal Cysts:

Class I: Simple cysts, 100% benign
Class II: Minimally complicated cyst, 100% benign
Class IIF: Minimally complicated cyst with suspicious features, follow up scan recommended, most likely benign
Class III: Moderately complicated or multiloculated cyst, 50% malignant, surgery recommended
Class IV: Cleary malignant lesion, surgery recommended

&GOUTALLIERThe Goutallier classification
> to quantify the amount of degeneration of the rotator cuff muscles, particularly in the context of rotator cuff tendon tears.
> It is based mainly on the percentage of atrophy and fatty degeneration of the involved muscle.

grade 0: normal muscle
grade 1: some fatty streaks
grade 2: less than 50% fatty muscle atrophy (<50%)
grade 3: 50% fatty muscle atrophy (=50%)
grade 4: greater than 50% fatty muscle atrophy (>50%)

> Increasing stage number indicates a more severe level of degeneration, with stage 3 and 4 correlated with poorer post-repair return to normal function, thus serving as a possible contraindication for surgical repair.

&NOEFXNOE fracture = naso-orbito-ethmoid fracures

> disrupting the confluence of the medial maxillary buttress with the upper transverse maxillary buttress as well as their posterior extensions along the medial orbital wall and floor
> increase the transverse distance between the medial orbital walls and the attachments of the medial canthi, resulting in telecanthus

Manson system
> Manson type I fracture:
-- the fractured piece is large
-- the medial canthal insertion around the lacrimal fossa is intact.
-- Accurate fixation of the large bone fragment will restore the canthal anatomy.

> Manson type II fracture:
-- there is comminution of the buttress
-- the canthus is attached to a small bone fragment.

> Manson type III fracture:
-- The type III pattern cannot be diagnosed with imaging
-- instead, it needs clinical examination to determine if the canthus is avulsed from the bone
&OCDSOsteochondroses:

Adams Disease -- the medial epicondyle of the humerus

Ahlback Disease -- spontaneous AVN of the femoral condyle in adults

Breck Disease-- AVN of the medial malleolus

Chandler Disease -- Idiopathic AVN of the femoral head in adult

Diaz Disease -- AVN of the talus

Freiberg Infraction -- AVN of the head of the 2nd or 3rd metatarsal

Iselin Disease -- AVN of base of 5th metatarsal apohysis in children

Keinbock Disease -- AVN of carpal lunate

Kohler Disease (child), AKA: Mueller-Weiss Syndrome (adult) -- AVN of tarsal navicular

LaNec Disease -- AVN of ischiopubic synchondrosis

Madelung Disease-- AVN of distal radial epihysis

Osgood-Schlatter Disease -- AVN of the tibial tubercle

Panner Disease -- AVN of capitellum of the humerus

Perthe Disease -- (Legg-Calve-Perthe Disease) -- AVN of femoral head in a child; idiopathic AVN of the femoral head in adult = Chandler Disease

Scheuermann Disease -- AVN of the ring epiphyses of the spine

Sever Disease -- AVN of the calcaneus

Sindig-Larsen-Johanssen Disease -- AVN of distal pole of patella

Theeman Disease-- AVN of phalangeal epiphysis

&PADTASC II criteria

=== aorto-iliac lesions===
Type A lesions:
？ Unilateral or bilateral stenoses of CIA
？ Unilateral or bilateral single short (<= 3cm) stenosis of EIA

Type B lesions:
？ Short (<= 3cm) stenosis of infrarenal aorta
？ Unilateral CIA occlusion
？ Single or multiple stenosis totaling 3-10 cm involving the EIA not extending into the CFA
？ Unilateral EIA occlusion not involving the origins of internal iliac or CFA

Type C lesions:
？ Bilateral CIA occlusions
？ Bilateral EIA stenoses 3-10 cm long not extending into the CFA
？ Unilateral EIA stenosis extending into the CFA
？ Unilateral EIA occlusion that involves the origins of internal iliac and/or CFA
？ Heavily calci?ed unilateral EIA occlusion with or without involvement of origins of ingins of internal iliac and/or CFA

Type D lesions:
？ Infra-renal aorloiliac occlusion
？ Diffuse disease involving the aorta and both iliac arteries requiring treatment
？ Diffuse multiple stenoses involving the unilateral CIA, EIA, and CFA
？ Unilateral occlusion of both CIA and EIA
？ Bilateral occilisions of EIA
？ Iliac stenoses in patients with AAA requiring treatment and not amenable to endograft placement or other lesions requiring open aortic or iliac surgery

=== femoral popliteal lesions ===

Type A lesions:
？ Single stenosis <= 10 cm in length
？ Single occlusion <= 5 cm in length

Type B lesions:
？ Multiple lesions (stenoses or occlusions), each <= 5 cm
？ Unilateral CIA occlusion <= 15 cm not involving infrageniculate popliteal artery
？ Single or multiple lesions in the absence of continuous tibial vessels to improve in?ow for a distal bypass
？ Heavily calci?ed occlusion <= 5 cm in length
？ Single popliteal stenosis

Type C lesions:
？ Multiple stenoses or occlusions totaling > 15 cm with or without heavy calci?cation
？ Recurrent stenoses or occlusions that need treatment after two endovascular interventions

Type D lesions:
？ Chronic total occlusions of CFA or SFA (>20 CM, involving the popliteal artery)
？ Chronic total occlusion of popliteal artery and proximel trifurcation vessels

&SHO-MUSCLESupraspinatus muscle atrophy on MRI: Thomazeau classification
Thomazeau et al, Acta Orthop Scand, 67(3): 264-68, 1996

Stage 1: Normal/ slight atrophy Occupation ratio(1.00-0.60)
Stage 2: Moderate atrophy Occupation ratio(0.60-0.40)
Stage 3: Severe atrophy Occupation ratio(<0.40)

Occupation ratio R = S1 / S2
S1= surface of supraspinatus muscle
S2= surface of entire supraspinatus fossa

Measurement on the scapular cut at level of medial border of spine of scapula

--

Fatty degeneration of cuff muscles: Goutallier's classification using CT scan
Goutallier et al, CORR, 304:78-83, 1994

Prognostic importance. Stages 3 and 4 have less chance of return to function

Stage 0 - Normal muscle
Stage 1 - Some fatty streaks
Stage 2 - Less than 50% fatty muscle atrophy
Stage 3 - 50% fatty muscle atrophy
Stage 4 - Greater than 50% fatty muscle atrophy

&SINGH-INDEXBony Trabeculae of the Proximal Femur:
- Ward''s Triangle
- Greater Trochanteric Group
- Secondary Compressive Group
- Secondary Tensile Group
- Principal Tensile Group
- Principal Compressive Group
Singh et. al. JBJS. 1970 (52-A) 457-467;

- Grade VI:
- all normal trabecular groups are visible
- upper end of femur seems to be completely occupied by cancellous bone;
- Grade V:
- principal tensile & principal compressive trabeculae is accentuated;
- Ward''s triangle appears prominent;
- Grade IV:
- principal tensile trabeculae are markedly reduced but can still be traced from lateral cortex to upper part of the femoral neck;
- Grade III:
- there is a break in the continuity of the principal tensile trabeculae opposite the greater trochanter;
- this grade indicates definite osteoporosis;
- Grade II:
- only principal compressive trabeculae stand out prominently;
- remaining trabeculae have been essentially absorbed;
- Grade I:
- principal compressive trabeculae are markedly reduced in number and are no longer prominent;
&SINUS_X-RAY== Waters view ==
> Occipito Mental
> the lines of Dolan and the elephants of Rogers
> Shows orbits, maxillary sinuses, zygomatic-frontal suture, mastoid air cells
> clear view of maxillary sinuses
> shows an orbital floor fx
> Tripod fx: arch of the zygomatic bone, zygomatic process of frontal bone, zygomatic process of maxillary bone

** Orbital (-) fracture: local nasal bone fracture, zygomatic arch fracture, and the LeFort I fracture

== Caldwell view ==
> PA 15°
> Shows orbits, ethmoid sinuses, frontal sinuses
> Can demonstrate medial (ethmoid) blowout fractures


== Lateral view ==
> Sphenoid sinus
> Sella turcica
> Cribriform plate


== Submentovertex (aka Base) ==
> Zygomatic arch, Lateral wall of orbit, Sphenoid sinuses
> Underpenetrated or “light” view is best for zygomatic arch fx



== Rhese (aka Oblique or Foramen) ==
> PA 15° + oblique 53°
> can show unilateral foramen enlargement (e.g., aneurysm, tumor, or rarely fx)

&TFCCPalmer classification

== traumatic injuries (Palmer class I)

IA : Perforation or traumatic tear of the TFC disc proper
IB : Ulnar avulsion of the TFC complex with or without associated ulnar styloid fracture
IC : Distal avulsions of the TFC complex through its lunate attachment (the ulnolunate ligament) or its triquetrum attachment (the ulnotriquetral ligament)
ID : Radial avulsions at the level of the distal sigmoid notch with or without associated sigmoid notch fracture


== degenerative injuries (Palmer class II).

IIA : TFC complex wear.
IIB : TFC complex wear and lunate, triquetrum, and possibly ulnar chondromalacia.
IIC : TFC complex perforation and lunate, triquetrum, and possibly ulnar chondromalacia.
IID : TFC complex perforation and lunate, triquetrum, and ulnar chondromalacia and lunotriquetral ligament perforation.
IIE : TFC complex perforation and lunate, triquetrum, and ulnar chondromalacia, lunotriquetral perforation, and ulnocarpal arthritis.
&UT/POSITIONPosition tipped
= "anteverted": tipped forward
= "retroverted": tipped backwards

Position of fundus
= "anteflexed": the fundus is pointing forward relative to the cervix. Anterior of uterus is concave.
= "retroflexed": the fundus is pointing backwards. Anterior of uterus is convex.

MUSCLE MASS MEASUREMENT:
> Lean mass of left arm (Kg) =
> Lean mass of right arm (Kg) =
> Lean mass of left leg (Kg) =
> Lean mass of right leg (Kg) =

> Height (m) =

> ASM index (Kg / m^2) =


> The ASM index indicates low muscle mass. Please correlate with the clinical condition for the diagnosis of sarcopenia.
> The ASM index indicates no low muscle mass.


REMARK:
> Appendicular skeletal mass (ASM) = the sum of the muscle masses of the four limbs.
> ASM index (Kg / m^2) = ASM / height^2
> The cutoff values for muscle mass measurement are 7.0 kg/m2 for men and 5.4 kg/m2 for women by using dual X-ray absorptiometry.

REFERENCE:
> Chen LK, et al. Sarcopenia in Asia: Consensus Report of the Asian Working Group for Sarcopenia. J Am Med Dir Assoc 2014;15:95-101.

DXA/LSC--

REMARK:
The least significant change (LSC) is the least amount of BMD change that can be considered statistically significant.

Using the Hologic DXA system, the LSC data in Taipei Veterans General Hospital list as below:
> lumbar spine: 0.031 g/cm2
> right hip: 0.038 g/cm2
> left hip: 0.033 g/cm2

Subtract the recent BMD result from the one used for comparison. If the difference is the same or greater than the LSC, then the change is considered to be statistically significant.

GASTRIC_LNThe Japanese Research Society for the study of gastric cancer published a manual in 1963 standardizing LND and pathologic evaluations for GC; these guidelines recognized 16 different LN stations that surround the stomach.

These 16 nodal stations are grouped according to the location and extension of the primary tumor (N0-N4) and the extent of lymphadenectomy is classified according the level of LND ( D1-D4).
--
In D1 dissections only the perigastric nodes directly attached along the lesser and greater curvatures (stations 1-6, N1 level):

1 RT cardia LNs
2 LT cardia LNs
3 LNs along the lesser curvature
4 LNs along the greater curvature

4sa: LNs along the short gastric vessels
4sb: LNs along the LT gastroepiploic vessels
4d: LNs along the RT gastroepiploic vessels

5 Suprapyloric LNs
6 Infrapyloric LNs

An incomplete N1 dissection is labelled a D0 lymphadenectomy.
--
D2 dissections (N2 level) add the removal of nodes along the

LT gastric artery (station 7),
common hepatic artery (station 8),
celiac trunk (station 9),
splenic hilus,
and splenic artery (station 10 and 11).
--
D3 dissections include the dissection of LNs at stations 12 through 14, along the hepatoduodenal ligament and the root of the mesentery (N3 level):

12 LNs in the hepatoduodenal ligament
13 LNs on the posterior surface of the head of the pancreas
14 LNs at the root of the mesentery

14A LNs along the superior mesenteric artery
14V LNs along the superior mesenteric vein
--
Finally D4 resections add the stations 15 and 16 in the para-aortic and the paracolic region (N4 level)

JJ/LKLeft percutaneous nephrostomy and antegrade double-J ureteral stent insertion were performed with patient lying on prone position:

> Under sonographic and fluoroscopic guidance, we inserted a 18-gauge PTC needle into left lower calyx and introduced a 150-cm/0.035-inch guidewire via PTC needle into left ureter.
> The tract was dilated by 9-Fr. dilator and secured by a 8-Fr. long sheath.
> Antegrade pyelography was performed with contrast medium injection via 4-Fr. KMP angiocatheter, revealing that

> Under fluoroscopic guidance, the 150-cm/0.035-inch guidewire was sent forward into urinary bladder.
> Then, a
24-
26-
cm/6-Fr. double-J stent was placed into the ureter via percutaneous antegrade route.
> Finally, a new 8-Fr. pigtail catheter is inserted along the guidewire into the renal pelvis.
> Antegrade pyelography revealed contrast jet at distal end of double-J stent.
> The urine was drained out via pigtail catheter smoothly.
> The procedure was performed smoothly without immediate complications, and the patient stood it well.

hydronephrosis of right kidney.

> The tract was dilated by 9-Fr. dilator and secured by a 8-Fr. long sheath.

> Then, a
24-
26-
cm/6-Fr. double-J stent was placed into the ureter via percutaneous antegrade route.
> Finally, a new 8-Fr. pigtail catheter was inserted along the guidewire into the renal pelvis.
> Antegrade pyelography revealed contrast jet at distal end of double-J stent.
> The urine was drained out via the catheter smoothly.

PCNL/LKLeft percutaneous nephrostomy for lithotomy was performed smoothly with patient lying on prone position:

> Sonography revealed stones in left renal pelvis and lower calyces and no hydronephrosis.
> Under both sonographic and fluoro-guidance, we punctured the lower pole of the stone by 18-gauge PTC needle, and opacified the collecting system by diluted contrast medium injection.
> After negotiating the 80-cm/0.035-inch guidewire through the stone with curving in the dilated upper calyx, the tract was dilated by 9-Fr. dilator and secured by a 8-Fr. long sheath.
> Another 150-cm/0.035-inch guidewire was inserted into upper calyx.
> A 8-Fr. pigtail catheter was inserted along the 80-cm wire with the tip curving in the dilated upper calyx.
> The tract was then dilated and secured by a 24-Fr./10-cm Uroforce balloon catheter.
> The procedure was performed smoothly without immediate complications, and the patient stood it well.

PG/Placement of percutaneous gastrostomy:

> S/p NG tube insertion with the tip in the stomach.
> After intravenous injection with 1 amp buscopan as gastric hypotonic agent and gas inflation with about 400-mL room air for gastric distention, we directly puncture the stomach at anterior wall of low body.
> A Bentson guidewire was inserted into stomach via the puncture needle.
> After dilating the tract with a 12-Fr. fascia dilator, a 12-Fr. Dawson-Mueller catheter was inserted to high body as feeding tube. The patient stood the whole course well and sent back to ward in stable condition.

> The patient is followed on

2nd day.

> The patient may begin gastrostomy feeding.
